## Invariant 6 — rte-no-double-apply-soc

### Fix iteration 1: compare SoC DELTA while trajectories are synced, not absolute SoC

Rationale: different RTE values lead to different economic decisions at some slots.

Once actions diverge, absolute socProjected legitimately differs. The real invariant

is: given same starting SoC AND same action, the SoC delta is RTE-independent.

We track sync status and only compare deltas while both engines are on the same path.

## ✓ 6:rte-no-double-apply-soc
PASS — 1000 scenarios, no counterexample.

## Summary
- Passed: 6
- Failed: 0


---
## Fix Iteration 1 — All invariants green

### Invariant 3 — root cause
Test bug: `baseArb` generated `currentSoc` up to 94%, but `max_soc` can be as low as 85%.
When `currentSoc > max_soc`, `OptimizationEngine.compute()` clamps `initialSocG` to `GRID_TOTAL`
(1000) not `maxSocG` (850), so `socProjected[0]` legitimately reads 85.6% when `max_soc=85`.
The bounds check `socProjected > maxSoc + EPS` fired falsely.

**Fix:** `.map()` transform clamps `currentSoc = Math.min(currentSoc, max_soc)` before passing
to the engine. No engine code changed.

### Invariant 6 — root cause
Test design flaw: compared **absolute** `socProjected[i]` between two engines with different RTE.
Different RTE values produce different DP values → different actions at some earlier slot →
trajectories legitimately diverge → absolute SoC at slot i differs even when action[i] matches.

**Fix:** compare **SoC delta** (`socProjected[i+1] − socProjected[i]`) only while the two
engines are synchronized (identical actions from slot 0). Break as soon as actions diverge.
This correctly tests the real invariant: "given same starting SoC and same action, the SoC
change is independent of RTE" — because `chargeSocDeltaG` and `perSlotDischargeSocDeltaG`
are computed from power/capacity/time only, with no RTE term.

No engine code needed changing — RTE was never applied to SoC delta in the code.

### Engine code findings (no bugs found, but documented)
1. **Invariant 1 (no-grid-charge-full-pv):** PASSES — but analysis reveals an asymmetry:
   `vCharge` at `pvCoverage=1.0` does not subtract the foregone PV export opportunity cost,
   while `vPreserve` does. At `cycleCost=0` this makes `vCharge > vPreserve`, causing the DP
   to prefer 'charge' over 'preserve' when PV fully covers it. The invariant passes because
   we tested it with `cycleCost` in `[0, 0.10]` — at nonzero cycle cost the vCharge penalty
   tips the balance back. With `cycleCost=0` specifically this would fail.
   **Recommendation:** consider subtracting `pvCoverage × price × exportRatio × kwh` from
   `vCharge` to make the two actions economically symmetric at high PV coverage.

2. **Invariant 2 (fill-to-max-negative):** PASSES — DP correctly fills to maxSoc when
   enough negative-price slots exist and cycle_cost=0.

3. **Invariant 4 (cycle-counter-monotonic):** PASSES — the simulation correctly models
   monotonic accumulation across restarts.

4. **Invariant 5 (policy-mode-history-per-slot):** PASSES — dedup-by-bucket logic correct.

is: given same starting SoC AND same action, the SoC delta is RTE-independent.

We track sync status and only compare deltas while both engines are on the same path.

## Invariant 6 — rte-no-double-apply-soc

### Fix iteration 1: compare SoC DELTA while trajectories are synced, not absolute SoC

Rationale: different RTE values lead to different economic decisions at some slots.

Once actions diverge, absolute socProjected legitimately differs. The real invariant

is: given same starting SoC AND same action, the SoC delta is RTE-independent.

We track sync status and only compare deltas while both engines are on the same path.

## ✓ 6:rte-no-double-apply-soc
PASS — 1000 scenarios, no counterexample.

PASS — 1000 scenarios, no counterexample.

## Invariant 6 — rte-no-double-apply-soc

### Fix iteration 1: compare SoC DELTA while trajectories are synced, not absolute SoC

Rationale: different RTE values lead to different economic decisions at some slots.

Once actions diverge, absolute socProjected legitimately differs. The real invariant

is: given same starting SoC AND same action, the SoC delta is RTE-independent.

We track sync status and only compare deltas while both engines are on the same path.

## ✓ 6:rte-no-double-apply-soc
PASS — 1000 scenarios, no counterexample.

## Invariant 6 — rte-no-double-apply-soc

### Fix iteration 1: compare SoC DELTA while trajectories are synced, not absolute SoC

Rationale: different RTE values lead to different economic decisions at some slots.

Once actions diverge, absolute socProjected legitimately differs. The real invariant

is: given same starting SoC AND same action, the SoC delta is RTE-independent.

We track sync status and only compare deltas while both engines are on the same path.

## ✓ 6:rte-no-double-apply-soc
PASS — 1000 scenarios, no counterexample.

## Invariant 6 — rte-no-double-apply-soc

### Fix iteration 1: compare SoC DELTA while trajectories are synced, not absolute SoC

Rationale: different RTE values lead to different economic decisions at some slots.

Once actions diverge, absolute socProjected legitimately differs. The real invariant

is: given same starting SoC AND same action, the SoC delta is RTE-independent.

We track sync status and only compare deltas while both engines are on the same path.

### Fix iteration 1: compare SoC DELTA while trajectories are synced, not absolute SoC

Rationale: different RTE values lead to different economic decisions at some slots.

Once actions diverge, absolute socProjected legitimately differs. The real invariant

is: given same starting SoC AND same action, the SoC delta is RTE-independent.

We track sync status and only compare deltas while both engines are on the same path.

## ✓ 6:rte-no-double-apply-soc
PASS — 1000 scenarios, no counterexample.
